## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv_dt) depends on position, velocity, and possibly time. The equation of motion typically combines restoring forces (functions of x), damping (functions of v), and possibly external driving (functions of t).

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic nonlinearity + damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (with periodic driving)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing equation)
- Van der Pol type: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinearity)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Damped pendulum: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (sinusoidal restoring + damping)
- Driven damped pendulum: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t)
- Quadratic-cubic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric potential)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * x**2 (position-dependent damping)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (nonlinear velocity damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric potential wells; even powers (x²) → asymmetric potentials
- Velocity terms proportional to (1 - x²)*v indicate self-excited oscillations (Van der Pol type nonlinear damping)
- Periodic driving forces appear as sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms additive to the restoring/damping terms
- Position-velocity coupling terms like x*v or x²*v suggest state-dependent damping or parametric effects
- Sinusoidal dependence on position sin(c*x) rather than polynomial suggests a periodic potential (pendulum-like systems)
- Absence of explicit time dependence indicates an autonomous system where energy is either conserved or monotonically dissipated
- Cubic position terms with sign opposite to the linear term (c0*x - c1*x³ with c0,c1>0) indicate a softening spring / double-well potential
- Odd velocity powers (v, v³) preserve time-reversal symmetry of dissipation, while even powers (v²) break it and indicate direction-dependent damping
